<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Hawaii</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">

</div>
<div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Not to be confused with <a href="/wiki/Hawaiki" title="Hawaiki">Hawaiki</a>.</div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">This article is about the U.S. state of Hawaii. For the island for which it is named, see <a href="/wiki/Hawaii_(island)" title="Hawaii (island)">Hawaii (island)</a>. For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Hawaii_(disambiguation)" title="Hawaii (disambiguation)">Hawaii (disambiguation)</a>.</div>

<p><b>Hawaii</b> (<span class="nowrap"><small>English:</small> <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'h' in 'hi'">h</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'w' in 'wind'">w</span><span title="/aɪ/: 'i' in 'tide'">aɪ</span><span title="/./: syllable break">.</span><span title="/iː/ or /ɪ/: 'y' in 'happy'">i</span></span>, -<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/j/: 'y' in 'yes'">j</span><span title="/iː/ or /ɪ/: 'y' in 'happy'">i</span></span>, -<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ʔ/: the catch in 'uh-oh'">ʔ</span><span title="/iː/ or /ɪ/: 'y' in 'happy'">i</span></span>/</a></span><small class="nowrap metadata"> (<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Hawaii.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></a> </span><a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e4/En-us-Hawaii.ogg" title="En-us-Hawaii.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><small title="English pronunciation respelling"><i>hə-<b>WY</b>-(y)ee</i></small></a>; <a href="/wiki/Hawaiian_language" title="Hawaiian language">Hawaiian</a>: <span lang="haw"><i><b>Hawai<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>i</b></i></span> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Hawaiian" title="Help:IPA/Hawaiian">[həˈvɐjʔi]</a></span>) is the 50th and most recent <a href="/wiki/U.S._state" title="U.S. state">state</a> to have joined the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States of America</a>, having received statehood on August 21, 1959.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[10]</a></sup> Hawaii is the only U.S. state located in <a href="/wiki/Oceania" title="Oceania">Oceania</a> and the only one composed entirely of islands. It is the northernmost island group in <a href="/wiki/Polynesia" title="Polynesia">Polynesia</a>, occupying most of an <a href="/wiki/Archipelago" title="Archipelago">archipelago</a> in the central <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific Ocean</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boehonbcn_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-boehonbcn-12">[11]</a></sup> Hawaii is the only U.S. state located outside <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a>.</p>
<p>The state encompasses nearly the entire volcanic <a href="/wiki/Hawaiian_Islands" title="Hawaiian Islands">Hawaiian archipelago</a>, which comprises hundreds of islands spread over 1,500 miles (2,400 km). At the southeastern end of the archipelago, the eight main islands are—in order from northwest to southeast: <a href="/wiki/Niihau" title="Niihau">Ni<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>ihau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kauai" title="Kauai">Kaua<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>i</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oahu" title="Oahu">O<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>ahu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Molokai" title="Molokai">Moloka<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>i</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lanai" title="Lanai">Lāna<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>i</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kahoolawe" title="Kahoolawe">Kaho<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>olawe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maui" title="Maui">Maui</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Hawaii_(island)" title="Hawaii (island)">Island of Hawai<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>i</a>. The last is the largest island in the group; it is often called the "Big Island" or "Hawai<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>i Island" to avoid confusion with the state or archipelago. The archipelago is physiographically and ethnologically part of the Polynesian subregion of Oceania.</p>
<p>Hawaii's diverse natural scenery, warm tropical climate, abundance of public beaches, oceanic surroundings, and active volcanoes make it a popular destination for tourists, surfers, biologists, and volcanologists. Because of its central location in the Pacific and 19th-century labor migration, Hawaii's culture is strongly influenced by North American and Asian cultures, in addition to its <a href="/wiki/Native_Hawaiians" title="Native Hawaiians">indigenous Hawaiian</a> culture. Hawaii has over a million permanent residents, along with many visitors and U.S. military personnel. Its capital is <a href="/wiki/Honolulu" title="Honolulu">Honolulu</a> on the island of O<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>ahu.</p>
<p>Hawaii is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_and_territories_by_area" title="List of U.S. states and territories by area">8th-smallest</a> and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_and_territories_by_population" title="List of U.S. states and territories by population">11th-least populous</a>, but the <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_by_population_density" title="List of U.S. states by population density">13th-most densely populated</a> of the fifty U.S. states. It is the only state with an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian_American" title="Asian American">Asian</a> <a href="/wiki/Plurality_(voting)" title="Plurality (voting)">plurality</a>. The state's coastline is about 750 miles (1,210 km) long, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_by_coastline" title="List of U.S. states by coastline">fourth longest in the U.S.</a> after the coastlines of Alaska, Florida, and California.</p>

<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span></h2>
<p>The state of Hawaii derives its name from the name of its largest island, <a href="/wiki/Hawaii_(island)" title="Hawaii (island)">Hawai<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>i</a>. A common Hawaiian explanation of the name of Hawai<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>i is that was named for <a href="/wiki/Hawaiiloa" title="Hawaiiloa">Hawai<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>iloa</a>, a legendary figure from Hawaiian myth. He is said to have discovered the islands when they were first settled.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Hawaiian_language" title="Hawaiian language">Hawaiian language</a> word <i>Hawai<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>i</i> is very similar to <a href="/wiki/Proto-Polynesian_language" title="Proto-Polynesian language">Proto-Polynesian</a> *<i>Sawaiki</i>, with the <a href="/wiki/Internal_reconstruction" title="Internal reconstruction">reconstructed</a> meaning "homeland".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[14]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cognate" title="Cognate">Cognates</a> of <i>Hawai<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>i</i> are found in other Polynesian languages, including <a href="/wiki/M%C4%81ori_language" title="Māori language">Māori</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Hawaiki" title="Hawaiki">Hawaiki</a></i>), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cook_Islands_Maori" title="Cook Islands Maori">Rarotongan</a> (<i>ʻAvaiki</i>) and <a href="/wiki/Samoan_language" title="Samoan language">Samoan</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Savai%27i" title="Savai'i">Savai<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>i</a></i>) . According to linguists Pukui and Elbert,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[15]</a></sup> "[e]lsewhere in Polynesia, Hawai<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>i or a cognate is the name of the underworld or of the ancestral home, but in Hawaii, the name has no meaning".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[16]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Spelling_of_state_name">Spelling of state name</span></h3>
<p>A somewhat divisive political issue arose in 1978 when the Constitution of the State of Hawaii added Hawaiian as a second official state language.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[17]</a></sup> The title of the state constitution is <i>The Constitution of the State of Hawaii</i>. Article<span class="nowrap"> </span>XV, Section<span class="nowrap"> </span>1 of the Constitution uses <i>The State of Hawaii</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[18]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Diacritic" title="Diacritic">Diacritics</a> were not used because the document, drafted in 1949,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[19]</a></sup> predates the use of the <a href="/wiki/%CA%BBOkina" title="ʻOkina">okina</a> (<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>) and the <a href="/wiki/Macron_(diacritic)" title="Macron (diacritic)">kahakō</a> in modern Hawaiian orthography. The exact spelling of the state's name in the Hawaiian language is <i>Hawai<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>i</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[b]</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Hawaii_Admission_Act" title="Hawaii Admission Act">Hawaii Admission Act</a> that granted Hawaiian statehood, the federal government recognized <i>Hawaii</i> as the official state name. Official government publications, department and office titles, and the <a href="/wiki/Seal_of_Hawaii" title="Seal of Hawaii">Seal of Hawaii</a> use the traditional spelling with no symbols for glottal stops or vowel length.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[20]</a></sup> In contrast, the National and State Parks Services, the University of Hawai<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>i and some private enterprises implement these symbols. No precedent for changes to U.S. state names exists since the adoption of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Constitution" title="United States Constitution">United States Constitution</a> in 1789. However, the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Massachusetts" title="Constitution of Massachusetts">Constitution of Massachusetts</a> formally changed the <i>Province of Massachusetts Bay</i> to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Massachusetts" title="Commonwealth of Massachusetts">Commonwealth of Massachusetts</a> in 1780, and in 1819 the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Territory_of_Arkansaw" title="Territory of Arkansaw">Territory of Arkansaw</a> was created but was later admitted to statehood as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_of_Arkansas" title="State of Arkansas">State of Arkansas</a>.</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography_and_environment"><span id="Geography"></span>Geography and environment</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hawaiian_Islands" title="Hawaiian Islands">Hawaiian Islands</a></div>
<p>There are eight main Hawaiian islands, seven of which are permanently inhabited. The island of Ni<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>ihau is privately managed by brothers Bruce and <a href="/wiki/Keith_Robinson_(environmentalist)" title="Keith Robinson (environmentalist)">Keith Robinson</a>; access is restricted to those who have permission from the island's owners. Access to uninhabited <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kaho%CA%BBolawe" title="Kahoʻolawe">Kahoʻolawe</a> island is also restricted.</p>

<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Topography">Topography</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hawaii_in_Pacific_Ocean.png"><img alt="World map with Hawaiian islands in the middle" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="330" data-file-width="330" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Hawaii_in_Pacific_Ocean.png/220px-Hawaii_in_Pacific_Ocean.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/d2/Hawaii_in_Pacific_Ocean.png 1.5x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hawaii_in_Pacific_Ocean.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Hawaiian_Islands" title="Hawaiian Islands">Hawaiian Islands</a> are located in the North Pacific Ocean</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Hawaiian archipelago is located 2,000 mi (3,200 km) southwest of the contiguous United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[31]</a></sup> Hawaii is the southernmost U.S. state and the second westernmost after Alaska. Hawaii, along with Alaska, does not border any other U.S. state. It is the only U.S. state that is not geographically located in North America, the only state completely surrounded by water and that is entirely an archipelago, and the only state in which coffee is commercially cultivable.</p>
<p>In addition to the eight main islands, the state has many smaller islands and islets. <a href="/wiki/Ka%CA%BBula" title="Kaʻula">Ka<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>ula</a> is a small island near Ni<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>ihau. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Northwest_Hawaiian_Islands" title="Northwest Hawaiian Islands">Northwest Hawaiian Islands</a> is a group of nine small, older islands to the northwest of Kaua<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>i that extend from <a href="/wiki/Nihoa" title="Nihoa">Nihoa</a> to <a href="/wiki/Kure_Atoll" title="Kure Atoll">Kure Atoll</a>; these are remnants of once much larger volcanic mountains. Across the archipelago are around 130 small rocks and islets, such as <a href="/wiki/Molokini" title="Molokini">Molokini</a>, which are either volcanic, marine sedimentary or erosional in origin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>Hawaii's tallest mountain <a href="/wiki/Mauna_Kea" title="Mauna Kea">Mauna Kea</a> is 13,796 ft (4,205 m) above mean sea level;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[33]</a></sup> it is taller than <a href="/wiki/Mount_Everest" title="Mount Everest">Mount Everest</a> if measured from the base of the mountain, which lies on the floor of the Pacific Ocean and rises about 33,500 feet (10,200 m).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[34]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geology">Geology</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hawaii_hotspot" title="Hawaii hotspot">Hawaii hotspot</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:P%C4%81hoehoe_lava_meets_Pacific.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1772" data-file-width="2824" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/P%C4%81hoehoe_lava_meets_Pacific.jpg/220px-P%C4%81hoehoe_lava_meets_Pacific.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/P%C4%81hoehoe_lava_meets_Pacific.jpg/330px-P%C4%81hoehoe_lava_meets_Pacific.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/P%C4%81hoehoe_lava_meets_Pacific.jpg/440px-P%C4%81hoehoe_lava_meets_Pacific.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:P%C4%81hoehoe_lava_meets_Pacific.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Pāhoehoe, or smooth lava, spills into the Pacific Ocean, forming new rock off the coast of the Island of Hawaii.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Hawaiian islands were formed by volcanic activity initiated at an undersea <a href="/wiki/Magma" title="Magma">magma</a> source called the <a href="/wiki/Hawaii_hotspot" title="Hawaii hotspot">Hawaii hotspot</a>. The process is continuing to build islands; the <a href="/wiki/Plate_tectonics" title="Plate tectonics">tectonic plate</a> beneath much of the Pacific Ocean continually moves northwest and the hot spot remains stationary, slowly creating new volcanoes. Because of the hotspot's location, all currently active land volcanoes are located on the southern half of Hawaii Island. The newest volcano, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Loihi_Seamount" title="Loihi Seamount">Lō<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>ihi Seamount</a>, is located south of the coast of Hawaii Island.</p>
<p>The last volcanic eruption outside Hawaii Island occurred at <a href="/wiki/Haleakal%C4%81" title="Haleakalā">Haleakalā</a> on Maui before the late 18th<span class="nowrap"> </span>century, possibly hundreds of years earlier.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[35]</a></sup> In 1790, <a href="/wiki/1790_Footprints" title="1790 Footprints">Kīlauea exploded</a>; it was the deadliest eruption known to have occurred in the modern era in what is now the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[36]</a></sup> Up to 5,405 warriors and their families marching on <a href="/wiki/K%C4%ABlauea" title="Kīlauea">Kīlauea</a> were killed by the eruption.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[37]</a></sup> Volcanic activity and subsequent erosion have created impressive geological features. Hawaii Island has the <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_by_highest_point" title="List of islands by highest point">third-highest point</a> among the world's islands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[38]</a></sup></p>
<p>On the flanks of the volcanoes, slope instability has generated damaging earthquakes and related <a href="/wiki/Tsunami" title="Tsunami">tsunamis</a>, particularly in <a href="/wiki/1868_Hawaii_earthquake" title="1868 Hawaii earthquake">1868</a> and <a href="/wiki/1975_Hawaii_earthquake" title="1975 Hawaii earthquake">1975</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PTWC_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-PTWC-41">[39]</a></sup> Steep cliffs have been created by catastrophic <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Debris_avalanche" title="Debris avalanche">debris avalanches</a> on the submerged flanks of ocean island volcanoes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[41]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Flora_and_fauna">Flora and fauna</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Endemism_in_the_Hawaiian_Islands" title="Endemism in the Hawaiian Islands">Endemism in the Hawaiian Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_invasive_plant_species_in_Hawaii" title="List of invasive plant species in Hawaii">List of invasive plant species in Hawaii</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Corvus_hawaiiensis.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1537" data-file-width="1000" height="261" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Corvus_hawaiiensis.jpg/170px-Corvus_hawaiiensis.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Corvus_hawaiiensis.jpg/255px-Corvus_hawaiiensis.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Corvus_hawaiiensis.jpg/340px-Corvus_hawaiiensis.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Corvus_hawaiiensis.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>Corvus hawaiiensis</i>, the endemic <a href="/wiki/Hawaiian_crow" title="Hawaiian crow">Hawaiian crow</a> (<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>alalā), is extinct in the wild.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Because the islands of Hawaii are distant from other land habitats, life is thought to have arrived there by wind, waves (i.e. by ocean currents) and wings (i.e. birds, insects, and any seeds they may have carried on their feathers). This isolation, in combination with the diverse environment (including extreme altitudes, tropical climates, and arid shorelines), produced an array of endemic flora and fauna. Hawaii has more endangered species and has lost a higher percentage of its endemic species than any other U.S. state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[42]</a></sup> One endemic plant, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brighamia" title="Brighamia">Brighamia</a></i>, now requires hand-pollination because its natural pollinator is presumed to be extinct.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[43]</a></sup> The two species of <i>Brighamia</i>—<i>B. rockii</i> and <i>B. insignis</i>—are represented in the wild by around 120 individual plants. To ensure these plants set seed, biologists rappel down 3,000-foot (910 m) cliffs to brush pollen onto their stigmas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[44]</a></sup></p>
<p>The extant main islands of the archipelago have been above the surface of the ocean for fewer than 10<span class="nowrap"> </span>million years; a fraction of the time biological colonization and evolution have occurred there. The islands are well known for the environmental diversity that occurs on high mountains within a trade winds field. On a single island, the climate around the coasts can range from dry tropical (less than 20 inches or 510 millimeters annual rainfall) to wet tropical; on the slopes, environments range from tropical rainforest (more than 200 inches or 5,100 millimeters per year), through a temperate climate, to alpine conditions with a cold, dry climate. The rainy climate impacts soil development, which largely determines ground permeability, affecting the distribution of streams and wetlands.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Protected_areas">Protected areas</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hawaiian_monk_seal_at_French_Frigate_Shoals_07.jpg"><img alt=" A Hawaiian monk seal rests at French Frigate Shoals." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2736" data-file-width="3648" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Hawaiian_monk_seal_at_French_Frigate_Shoals_07.jpg/220px-Hawaiian_monk_seal_at_French_Frigate_Shoals_07.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Hawaiian_monk_seal_at_French_Frigate_Shoals_07.jpg/330px-Hawaiian_monk_seal_at_French_Frigate_Shoals_07.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Hawaiian_monk_seal_at_French_Frigate_Shoals_07.jpg/440px-Hawaiian_monk_seal_at_French_Frigate_Shoals_07.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hawaiian_monk_seal_at_French_Frigate_Shoals_07.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/French_Frigate_Shoals" title="French Frigate Shoals">French Frigate Shoals</a>, located in the <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_Hawaiian_Islands" title="Northwestern Hawaiian Islands">Northwestern Hawaiian Islands</a>, is protected as part of the <a href="/wiki/Papah%C4%81naumoku%C4%81kea_Marine_National_Monument" title="Papahānaumokuākea Marine National Monument">Papahānaumokuākea Marine National Monument</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Several areas in Hawaii are under the protection of the <a href="/wiki/National_Park_Service" title="National Park Service">National Park Service</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[45]</a></sup> Hawaii has two national parks: <a href="/wiki/Haleakal%C4%81_National_Park" title="Haleakalā National Park">Haleakalā National Park</a> located near <a href="/wiki/Kula,_Hawaii" title="Kula, Hawaii">Kula</a> on the island of Maui, which features the dormant volcano Haleakalā that formed east Maui, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hawaii_Volcanoes_National_Park" title="Hawaii Volcanoes National Park">Hawaii Volcanoes National Park</a> in the southeast region of the Hawai<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>i Island, which includes the active volcano Kīlauea and its rift zones.</p>
<p>There are three <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_historical_park" title="National historical park">national historical parks</a>; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kalaupapa_National_Historical_Park" title="Kalaupapa National Historical Park">Kalaupapa National Historical Park</a> in Kalaupapa, Moloka<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>i, the site of a former leper colony; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kaloko-Honokohau_National_Historical_Park" title="Kaloko-Honokohau National Historical Park">Kaloko-Honokōhau National Historical Park</a> in <a href="/wiki/Kailua,_Hawaii_County,_Hawaii" title="Kailua, Hawaii County, Hawaii">Kailua-Kona</a> on Hawai<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>i Island; and <a href="/wiki/Pu%CA%BBuhonua_o_H%C5%8Dnaunau_National_Historical_Park" title="Puʻuhonua o Hōnaunau National Historical Park">Pu<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>uhonua o Hōnaunau National Historical Park</a>, an ancient place of refuge on Hawai<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>i Island's west coast. Other areas under the control of the National Park Service include <a href="/wiki/Ala_Kahakai_National_Historic_Trail" title="Ala Kahakai National Historic Trail">Ala Kahakai National Historic Trail</a> on Hawai<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>i Island and the <a href="/wiki/USS_Arizona_Memorial" title="USS Arizona Memorial">USS <i>Arizona</i> Memorial</a> at <a href="/wiki/Pearl_Harbor" title="Pearl Harbor">Pearl Harbor</a> on O<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>ahu.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Papah%C4%81naumoku%C4%81kea_Marine_National_Monument" title="Papahānaumokuākea Marine National Monument">Papahānaumokuākea Marine National Monument</a> was proclaimed by President <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> on June 15, 2006. The monument covers roughly 140,000 square miles (360,000 km<sup>2</sup>) of reefs, atolls, and shallow and deep sea out to 50 miles (80 km) offshore in the Pacific Ocean—an area larger than all of the national parks in the U.S. combined.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[46]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Hawaii_tornadoes" title="List of Hawaii tornadoes">List of Hawaii tornadoes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Hawaii" title="Climate of Hawaii">Climate of Hawaii</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hawaje-NoRedLine.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2800" data-file-width="3600" height="171" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Hawaje-NoRedLine.jpg/220px-Hawaje-NoRedLine.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Hawaje-NoRedLine.jpg/330px-Hawaje-NoRedLine.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Hawaje-NoRedLine.jpg/440px-Hawaje-NoRedLine.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hawaje-NoRedLine.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A true-color satellite view of Hawaii shows that most of the vegetation on the islands grows on the northeast sides which face the wind. The silver glow around the southwest of the islands is the result of calmer waters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[47]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Hawaii's climate is typical for the tropics, although temperatures and humidity tend to be less extreme because of near-constant <a href="/wiki/Trade_winds" title="Trade winds">trade winds</a> from the east. Summer highs usually reach around 88 °F (31 °C) during the day, with the temperature reaching a low of 75 °F (24 °C) at night. Winter day temperatures are usually around 83 °F (28 °C); at low elevation they seldom dip below 65 °F (18 °C) at night. Snow, not usually associated with the tropics, falls at 13,800 feet (4,200 m) on Mauna Kea and <a href="/wiki/Mauna_Loa" title="Mauna Loa">Mauna Loa</a> on Hawaii Island in some winter months. Snow rarely falls on Haleakalā. <a href="/wiki/Mount_Waialeale" title="Mount Waialeale">Mount Wai<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>ale<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>ale</a> on Kaua<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>i has the second-highest average annual rainfall on Earth, about 460 inches (12,000 mm) per year. Most of Hawaii experiences only two seasons; the dry season runs from May to October and the wet season is from October to April.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[48]</a></sup></p>
<p>The warmest temperature recorded in the state, in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pahala" title="Pahala">Pahala</a> on April 27, 1931, is 100 °F (38 °C), making it tied with <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaska</a> as the lowest record high temperature observed in a U.S. state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-51">[49]</a></sup> Hawaii's record low temperature is 12 °F (−11 °C) observed in May<span class="nowrap"> </span>1979 on the summit of Mauna Kea. Hawaii is the only state to have never recorded sub-zero Fahrenheit temperatures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_51-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-51">[49]</a></sup></p>
<p>Climates vary considerably on each island; they can be divided into <a href="/wiki/Windward_and_leeward" title="Windward and leeward">windward and leeward</a> (<i>ko<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>olau</i> and <i>kona</i>, respectively) areas based upon location relative to the higher mountains. Windward sides face cloud cover.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Hawaii" title="History of Hawaii">History of Hawaii</a></div>
<table class="vertical-navbox nowraplinks" style="float:right;clear:right;width:22.0em;margin:0 0 1.0em 1.0em;background:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;padding:0.2em;border-spacing:0.4em 0;text-align:center;line-height:1.4em;font-size:88%;background-color: #FAFAFA; border: 1px solid #CCC;">

<li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:History_of_Hawaii&amp;action=edit"><abbr style="font-size: 100%; margin: 2px;" title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li>
</ul>

</table>
<p>Hawaii is one of four U.S. states—apart from the original thirteen, along with the <a href="/wiki/Vermont_Republic" title="Vermont Republic">Vermont Republic</a> (1791), the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Texas" title="Republic of Texas">Republic of Texas</a> (1845), and the <a href="/wiki/California_Republic" title="California Republic">California Republic</a> (1846)—that were independent nations prior to statehood. Along with Texas, Hawaii had formal, international <a href="/wiki/Diplomatic_recognition" title="Diplomatic recognition">diplomatic recognition</a> as a nation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[50]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hawaii" title="Kingdom of Hawaii">Kingdom of Hawai<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>i</a> was sovereign from 1810 until 1893 when <a href="/wiki/Overthrow_of_the_Kingdom_of_Hawaii" title="Overthrow of the Kingdom of Hawaii">the monarchy was overthrown</a> by resident American and European capitalists and landholders. Hawaii was an independent republic from 1894 until August 12, 1898, when it officially became a territory of the United States. Hawaii was admitted as a U.S. state on August 21, 1959.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[51]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="First_human_settlement_–_Ancient_Hawaiʻi_(800–1778)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="First_human_settlement_.E2.80.93_Ancient_Hawai.CA.BBi_.28800.E2.80.931778.29">First human settlement – Ancient Hawai<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>i (800–1778)</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Hawaii" title="Ancient Hawaii">Ancient Hawaii</a></div>
<p>Based on archaeological evidence, the earliest habitation of the Hawaiian Islands dates to around 300 CE, probably by Polynesian settlers from the <a href="/wiki/Marquesas_Islands" title="Marquesas Islands">Marquesas Islands</a>. A second wave of migration from <a href="/wiki/Raiatea" title="Raiatea">Raiatea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bora_Bora" title="Bora Bora">Bora Bora</a> took place in the 11th century. The date of the human discovery and habitation of the Hawaiian Islands is the subject of academic debate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[52]</a></sup> Some archaeologists and historians think it was a later wave of immigrants from <a href="/wiki/Tahiti" title="Tahiti">Tahiti</a> around 1000 CE who introduced a new line of high chiefs, the <a href="/wiki/Kapu" title="Kapu">kapu</a> system, the practice of human sacrifice, and the building of <i><a href="/wiki/Heiau" title="Heiau">heiau</a></i>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> This later immigration is detailed in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hawaiian_mythology" title="Hawaiian mythology">Hawaiian mythology</a> (<i>mo<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>olelo</i>) about <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pa%27ao" title="Pa'ao">Pa<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>ao</a>. Other authors say there is no archaeological or linguistic evidence for a later influx of Tahitian settlers and that Pa<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>ao must be regarded as a myth.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The history of the islands is marked by a slow, steady growth in population and the size of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chiefdoms" title="Chiefdoms">chiefdoms</a>, which grew to encompass whole islands. Local chiefs, called <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ali%27i" title="Ali'i">ali<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>i</a>, ruled their settlements, and launched wars to extend their influence and defend their communities from predatory rivals. Ancient Hawaii was a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Makaainana" title="Makaainana">caste</a>-based society, much like that of Hindus in India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[53]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_arrival">European arrival</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tereoboo,_King_of_Owyhee,_bringing_presents_to_Captain_Cook_by_John_Webber.jpg"><img alt="Drawing of single-masted sailboat with one spinnaker-shaped sail, carrying dozens of men, accompanied by at least four other canoes." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2977" data-file-width="4763" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Tereoboo%2C_King_of_Owyhee%2C_bringing_presents_to_Captain_Cook_by_John_Webber.jpg/220px-Tereoboo%2C_King_of_Owyhee%2C_bringing_presents_to_Captain_Cook_by_John_Webber.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Tereoboo%2C_King_of_Owyhee%2C_bringing_presents_to_Captain_Cook_by_John_Webber.jpg/330px-Tereoboo%2C_King_of_Owyhee%2C_bringing_presents_to_Captain_Cook_by_John_Webber.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Tereoboo%2C_King_of_Owyhee%2C_bringing_presents_to_Captain_Cook_by_John_Webber.jpg/440px-Tereoboo%2C_King_of_Owyhee%2C_bringing_presents_to_Captain_Cook_by_John_Webber.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tereoboo,_King_of_Owyhee,_bringing_presents_to_Captain_Cook_by_John_Webber.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Kalani%CA%BB%C5%8Dpu%CA%BBu" title="Kalaniʻōpuʻu">Kalaniʻōpuʻu</a>, King of Hawai<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>i, brings presents to <a href="/wiki/James_Cook" title="James Cook">Captain Cook</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>It is possible that <a href="/wiki/Conquistador" title="Conquistador">Spanish explorers</a> arrived in the Hawaiian Islands in the 16th century—200 years before Captain <a href="/wiki/James_Cook" title="James Cook">James Cook</a>'s first documented visit in 1778. <a href="/wiki/Ruy_L%C3%B3pez_de_Villalobos" title="Ruy López de Villalobos">Ruy López de Villalobos</a> commanded a fleet of six ships that left <a href="/wiki/Acapulco" title="Acapulco">Acapulco</a> in 1542 bound for the Philippines with a Spanish sailor named Juan Gaetano aboard as pilot. Depending on the interpretation, Gaetano's reports describe an encounter with either Hawai<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>i or the <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Islands" title="Marshall Islands">Marshall Islands</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kane_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kane-56">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[55]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="Blogs are not considered reliable sources. (January 2017)">better source needed</span></a></i>]</sup> If de Villalobos' crew spotted Hawai<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>i, Gaetano would be considered the first European to see the islands. Some scholars have dismissed these claims due to a lack of credibility.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[56]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p>Spanish archives contain a chart that depicts islands at the same latitude as Hawai<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>i but with a longitude ten degrees east of the islands. In this manuscript, the island of Maui is named <i>La Desgraciada</i> (The Unfortunate Island), and what appears to be Hawai<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>i Island is named <i>La Mesa</i> (The Table). Islands resembling Kahoolawe, Lanai, and Molokai are named <i>Los Monjes</i> (The Monks).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[58]</a></sup> For two-and-a-half centuries, <a href="/wiki/Manila_galleon" title="Manila galleon">Spanish galleons</a> crossed the Pacific from Mexico along a route that passed south of Hawai<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>i on their way to <a href="/wiki/Manila" title="Manila">Manila</a>. The exact route was kept secret to protect the Spanish trade monopoly against competing powers.</p>
<p>The 1778 arrival of British explorer <a href="/wiki/James_Cook" title="James Cook">James Cook</a> was the first documented contact by a European explorer with Hawaii. Cook named the archipelago as the Sandwich Islands in honor of his sponsor <a href="/wiki/John_Montagu,_4th_Earl_of_Sandwich" title="John Montagu, 4th Earl of Sandwich">John Montagu, 4th Earl of Sandwich</a>. Cook published the islands' location and rendered the native name as <i>Owyhee</i>. This spelling lives on in <a href="/wiki/Owyhee_County,_Idaho" title="Owyhee County, Idaho">Owyhee County</a>, <a href="/wiki/Idaho" title="Idaho">Idaho</a>. It was named after three native Hawaiian members of a trapping party who went missing in that area. The <a href="/wiki/Owyhee_Mountains" title="Owyhee Mountains">Owyhee Mountains</a> were also named for them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[59]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Entrevue_de_l%27expedition_de_M._Kotzebue_avec_le_roi_Tammeamea_dans_l%27ile_d%27Ovayhi,_Iles_Sandwich_(detailed).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="550" data-file-width="713" height="170" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Entrevue_de_l%27expedition_de_M._Kotzebue_avec_le_roi_Tammeamea_dans_l%27ile_d%27Ovayhi%2C_Iles_Sandwich_%28detailed%29.jpg/220px-Entrevue_de_l%27expedition_de_M._Kotzebue_avec_le_roi_Tammeamea_dans_l%27ile_d%27Ovayhi%2C_Iles_Sandwich_%28detailed%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Entrevue_de_l%27expedition_de_M._Kotzebue_avec_le_roi_Tammeamea_dans_l%27ile_d%27Ovayhi%2C_Iles_Sandwich_%28detailed%29.jpg/330px-Entrevue_de_l%27expedition_de_M._Kotzebue_avec_le_roi_Tammeamea_dans_l%27ile_d%27Ovayhi%2C_Iles_Sandwich_%28detailed%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Entrevue_de_l%27expedition_de_M._Kotzebue_avec_le_roi_Tammeamea_dans_l%27ile_d%27Ovayhi%2C_Iles_Sandwich_%28detailed%29.jpg/440px-Entrevue_de_l%27expedition_de_M._Kotzebue_avec_le_roi_Tammeamea_dans_l%27ile_d%27Ovayhi%2C_Iles_Sandwich_%28detailed%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Entrevue_de_l%27expedition_de_M._Kotzebue_avec_le_roi_Tammeamea_dans_l%27ile_d%27Ovayhi,_Iles_Sandwich_(detailed).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
King Kamehameha receiving <a href="/wiki/Otto_von_Kotzebue" title="Otto von Kotzebue">Otto von Kotzebue</a>'s Russian naval expedition. Drawing by <a href="/wiki/Louis_Choris" title="Louis Choris">Louis Choris</a> in 1816.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Cook visited the Hawaiian Islands twice. As he prepared for departure after his second visit in 1779, a quarrel ensued as Cook took temple idols and fencing as "firewood",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[60]</a></sup> and a minor chief and his men took a ship's boat. Cook abducted the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alii_Aimoku_of_Hawaii" title="Alii Aimoku of Hawaii">King of Hawai<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>i Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kalani%CA%BB%C5%8Dpu%CA%BBu" title="Kalaniʻōpuʻu">Kalani<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>ōpu<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>u</a>, and held him for ransom aboard his ship in order to gain return of Cook's boat. This tactic had worked in Tahiti and other islands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[61]</a></sup> Instead, Kalani<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>ōpu<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>u's supporters fought back, killing Cook and four marines as Cook's party retreated along the beach to their ship. They departed without the ship's boat.</p>
<p>After Cook's visit and the publication of several books relating his voyages, the Hawaiian islands attracted many European visitors: explorers, traders, and eventually whalers, who found the islands to be a convenient harbor and source of supplies. Early British influence can be seen in the design of the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Hawaii" title="Flag of Hawaii">flag of Hawai<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>i</a>, which bears the <a href="/wiki/Union_Jack" title="Union Jack">Union Jack</a> in the top-left corner. These visitors introduced diseases to the once-isolated islands, causing the Hawaiian population to drop precipitously.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EB_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-EB-64">[62]</a></sup> Native Hawaiians had no resistance to Eurasian diseases, such as <a href="/wiki/Influenza" title="Influenza">influenza</a>, <a href="/wiki/Smallpox" title="Smallpox">smallpox</a> and <a href="/wiki/Measles" title="Measles">measles</a>. By 1820, disease, famine and wars between the chiefs killed more than half of the Native Hawaiian population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[63]</a></sup> During the 1850s, measles killed a fifth of Hawaii's people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[64]</a></sup></p>
<p>Historical records indicated the earliest Chinese immigrants to Hawaii originated from <a href="/wiki/Guangdong" title="Guangdong">Guangdong Province</a>; a few sailors arrived in 1778 with Captain Cook's journey and more arrived in 1789 with an American trader, who settled in Hawaii in the late 18th century. It appears that leprosy was introduced by Chinese workers by 1830; as with the other new infectious diseases, it proved damaging to the Hawaiians.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span id="Kingdom_of_Hawaiʻi"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Kingdom_of_Hawai.CA.BBi">Kingdom of Hawai<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>i</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hawaii" title="Kingdom of Hawaii">Kingdom of Hawaii</a></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="House_of_Kamehameha">House of Kamehameha</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kamehameha_I.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2808" data-file-width="2040" height="234" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Kamehameha_I.png/170px-Kamehameha_I.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Kamehameha_I.png/255px-Kamehameha_I.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Kamehameha_I.png/340px-Kamehameha_I.png 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kamehameha_I.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Kamehameha I conquered the Hawaiian Islands and established a unified monarchy across the archipelago.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During the 1780s and 1790s, chiefs often fought for power. After a series of battles that ended in 1795, all inhabited islands were subjugated under a single ruler, who became known as <a href="/wiki/Kamehameha_I" title="Kamehameha I">King Kamehameha the Great</a>. He established the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Kamehameha" title="House of Kamehameha">House of Kamehameha</a>, a dynasty that ruled the kingdom until 1872.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[65]</a></sup></p>
<p>After <a href="/wiki/Kamehameha_II" title="Kamehameha II">Kamehameha II</a> inherited the throne in 1819, American Protestant missionaries to Hawaii converted many Hawaiians to Christianity. They used their influence to end many traditional practices of the people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[67]</a></sup> During the reign of King <a href="/wiki/Kamehameha_III" title="Kamehameha III">Kamehameha III</a>, Hawai'i turned into a Christian monarchy with the signing of the <a href="/wiki/1840_Constitution_of_the_Kingdom_of_Hawaii" title="1840 Constitution of the Kingdom of Hawaii">1840 Constitution</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[68]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hiram_Bingham_I" title="Hiram Bingham I">Hiram Bingham I</a>, a prominent Protestant missionary, was a trusted adviser to the monarchy during this period. Other missionaries and their descendants became active in commercial and political affairs, leading to conflicts between the monarchy and its restive American subjects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[69]</a></sup> Catholic and Mormon missionaries were also active in the kingdom, but they converted a minority of the Native Hawaiian population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[72]</a></sup> Missionaries from each major group administered to the leper colony at Kalaupapa on Moloka<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>i, which was established in 1866 and operated well into the 20th century. The best known were <a href="/wiki/Father_Damien" title="Father Damien">Father Damien</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mother_Marianne_Cope" title="Mother Marianne Cope">Mother Marianne Cope</a>, both of whom were canonized in the early 21st century as Roman <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catholic_saints" title="Catholic saints">Catholic saints</a>.</p>
<p>The death of the bachelor <a href="/wiki/Kamehameha_V" title="Kamehameha V">King Kamehameha V</a>—who did not name an heir—resulted in the popular election of <a href="/wiki/Lunalilo" title="Lunalilo">Lunalilo</a> over <a href="/wiki/Kal%C4%81kaua" title="Kalākaua">Kalākaua</a>. Lunalilo died the next year, also without naming an heir. In 1874, the election was contested within the legislature between Kalākaua and <a href="/wiki/Queen_Emma_of_Hawaii" title="Queen Emma of Hawaii">Emma, Queen Consort of Kamehameha IV</a>. After riots broke out, the United States and Britain landed troops on the islands to restore order. <a href="/wiki/Kal%C4%81kaua" title="Kalākaua">King Kalākaua</a> was chosen as monarch by the <a href="/wiki/Legislature_of_the_Kingdom_of_Hawaii" title="Legislature of the Kingdom of Hawaii">Legislative Assembly</a> by a vote of 39 to 6 on February 12, 1874.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[73]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1887_Constitution_and_overthrow_preparations">1887 Constitution and overthrow preparations</span></h4>
<p>In 1887, Kalākaua was forced to sign the <a href="/wiki/1887_Constitution_of_the_Kingdom_of_Hawaii" title="1887 Constitution of the Kingdom of Hawaii">1887 Constitution of the Kingdom of Hawaii</a>. Drafted by white businessmen and lawyers, the document stripped the king of much of his authority. It established a property qualification for voting that effectively disenfranchised most Hawaiians and immigrant laborers and favored the wealthier, white elite. Resident whites were allowed to vote but resident Asians were not. As the 1887 Constitution was signed under threat of violence, it is known as the Bayonet Constitution. King Kalākaua, reduced to a figurehead, reigned until his death in 1891. His sister, Queen <a href="/wiki/Liliuokalani" title="Liliuokalani">Lili<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>uokalani</a>, succeeded him; she was the last monarch of Hawai<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>i.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[74]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1893, Queen Lili<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>uokalani announced plans for a new constitution to proclaim herself an absolute monarch. On January 14, 1893, a group of mostly Euro-American business leaders and residents formed the <a href="/wiki/Committee_of_Safety_(Hawaii)" title="Committee of Safety (Hawaii)">Committee of Safety</a> to stage a <a href="/wiki/Overthrow_of_the_Kingdom_of_Hawaii" title="Overthrow of the Kingdom of Hawaii">coup d'état</a> against the kingdom and seek annexation by the United States. United States Government Minister <a href="/wiki/John_L._Stevens" title="John L. Stevens">John L. Stevens</a>, responding to a request from the Committee of Safety, summoned a company of U.S. Marines. The Queen's soldiers did not resist. According to historian William Russ, the monarchy was unable to protect itself.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Adam_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-Adam-77">[75]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="Overthrow_of_1893_–_the_Republic_of_Hawaii_(1894–1898)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Overthrow_of_1893_.E2.80.93_the_Republic_of_Hawaii_.281894.E2.80.931898.29">Overthrow of 1893 – the Republic of Hawaii (1894–1898)</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Overthrow_of_the_Kingdom_of_Hawaii" title="Overthrow of the Kingdom of Hawaii">Overthrow of the Kingdom of Hawaii</a> and <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Hawaii" title="Republic of Hawaii">Republic of Hawaii</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Hawaiian_sovereignty_movement_groups#Historical_.E2.80.93_Royalist_Organizations_.28from_1880s.29" title="List of Hawaiian sovereignty movement groups">List of Hawaiian sovereignty movement groups § Historical – Royalist Organizations (from 1880s)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Liliuokalani_in_1891,_USC_Libraries.jpg"><img alt="Queen Liliʻuokalani, seated inside ʻIolani Palace." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="8461" data-file-width="5427" height="343" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Liliuokalani_in_1891%2C_USC_Libraries.jpg/220px-Liliuokalani_in_1891%2C_USC_Libraries.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Liliuokalani_in_1891%2C_USC_Libraries.jpg/330px-Liliuokalani_in_1891%2C_USC_Libraries.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Liliuokalani_in_1891%2C_USC_Libraries.jpg/440px-Liliuokalani_in_1891%2C_USC_Libraries.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Liliuokalani_in_1891,_USC_Libraries.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Liliuokalani" title="Liliuokalani">Queen Lili<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>uokalani</a>, the last reigning monarch of the Hawaiian Kingdom.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NORTHEAST_FACADE_-_Iolani_Palace,_King_and_Richards_Streets,_Honolulu,_Honolulu_County,_HI_HABS_HI,2-HONLU,8-7.tif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3432" data-file-width="4818" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/NORTHEAST_FACADE_-_Iolani_Palace%2C_King_and_Richards_Streets%2C_Honolulu%2C_Honolulu_County%2C_HI_HABS_HI%2C2-HONLU%2C8-7.tif/lossy-page1-220px-NORTHEAST_FACADE_-_Iolani_Palace%2C_King_and_Richards_Streets%2C_Honolulu%2C_Honolulu_County%2C_HI_HABS_HI%2C2-HONLU%2C8-7.tif.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/NORTHEAST_FACADE_-_Iolani_Palace%2C_King_and_Richards_Streets%2C_Honolulu%2C_Honolulu_County%2C_HI_HABS_HI%2C2-HONLU%2C8-7.tif/lossy-page1-330px-NORTHEAST_FACADE_-_Iolani_Palace%2C_King_and_Richards_Streets%2C_Honolulu%2C_Honolulu_County%2C_HI_HABS_HI%2C2-HONLU%2C8-7.tif.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/NORTHEAST_FACADE_-_Iolani_Palace%2C_King_and_Richards_Streets%2C_Honolulu%2C_Honolulu_County%2C_HI_HABS_HI%2C2-HONLU%2C8-7.tif/lossy-page1-440px-NORTHEAST_FACADE_-_Iolani_Palace%2C_King_and_Richards_Streets%2C_Honolulu%2C_Honolulu_County%2C_HI_HABS_HI%2C2-HONLU%2C8-7.tif.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NORTHEAST_FACADE_-_Iolani_Palace,_King_and_Richards_Streets,_Honolulu,_Honolulu_County,_HI_HABS_HI,2-HONLU,8-7.tif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iolani_Palace" title="Iolani Palace"><span class="unicode">ʻ</span>Iolani Palace</a> in <a href="/wiki/Honolulu" title="Honolulu">Honolulu</a>, formerly the residence of the Hawaiian monarch, was the capitol of the Republic of Hawaii.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In January 1893, Queen Lili<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>uokalani was overthrown and replaced by a provisional government composed of members of the Committee of Safety. Lawyer <a href="/wiki/Sanford_B._Dole" title="Sanford B. Dole">Sanford B. Dole</a>, a citizen of Hawaii, became President of the Republic when the <a href="/wiki/Provisional_Government_of_Hawaii" title="Provisional Government of Hawaii">Provisional Government of Hawaii</a> ended on July 4, 1894. Controversy ensued in the following years as the Queen tried to regain her throne. The administration of President <a href="/wiki/Grover_Cleveland" title="Grover Cleveland">Grover Cleveland</a> commissioned the <a href="/wiki/Blount_Report" title="Blount Report">Blount Report</a>, which concluded that the removal of Lili<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>uokalani had been illegal. The U.S. government first demanded that Queen Lili<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>uokalani be reinstated, but the Provisional Government refused.</p>
<p>Congress conducted an independent investigation, and on February 26, 1894, submitted the <a href="/wiki/Morgan_Report" title="Morgan Report">Morgan Report</a>, which found all parties, including Minister Stevens—with the exception of the Queen—"not guilty" and not responsible for the coup.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[76]</a></sup> Partisans on both sides of the debate questioned the accuracy and impartiality of both the Blount and Morgan reports over the events of 1893.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Adam_77-1"><a href="#cite_note-Adam-77">[75]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[77]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[78]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDAICS_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-HDAICS-81">[79]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1993, the US Congress passed a joint <a href="/wiki/Apology_Resolution" title="Apology Resolution">Apology Resolution</a> regarding the overthrow; it was signed by President <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">Bill Clinton</a>. The resolution did not apologize and did not say the overthrow was illegal. It, ""acknowledges that the overthrow of the Kingdom of Hawaii occurred with the active participation of agents and citizens of the United States and further acknowledges that the Native Hawaiian people never directly relinquished to the United States their claims to their inherent sovereignty as a people over their national lands, either through the Kingdom of Hawaii or through a plebiscite or referendum". <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDAICS_81-1"><a href="#cite_note-HDAICS-81">[79]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span id="Annexation_–_the_Territory_of_Hawaii_(1898–1959)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Annexation_.E2.80.93_the_Territory_of_Hawaii_.281898.E2.80.931959.29"><span id="annexation"></span>Annexation – the Territory of Hawaii (1898–1959)</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Territory_of_Hawaii" title="Territory of Hawaii">Territory of Hawaii</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1899BalanceCartoon.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="622" data-file-width="428" height="320" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/1899BalanceCartoon.jpg/220px-1899BalanceCartoon.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/1899BalanceCartoon.jpg/330px-1899BalanceCartoon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/46/1899BalanceCartoon.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1899BalanceCartoon.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
In 1899 Uncle Sam balances his new possessions which are depicted as savage children. The figures are <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>, Hawaii, <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a> and "Lad robes" (the <a href="/wiki/Mariana_Islands" title="Mariana Islands">Mariana Islands</a>).</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After <a href="/wiki/William_McKinley" title="William McKinley">William McKinley</a> won the 1896 U.S. presidential election, advocates pressed to annex the Republic of Hawaii. The previous president, Grover Cleveland, was a friend of Queen Lili<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>uokalani. McKinley was open to persuasion by U.S. expansionists and by annexationists from Hawai<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>i. He met with three annexationists: <a href="/wiki/Lorrin_A._Thurston" title="Lorrin A. Thurston">Lorrin A. Thurston</a>, Francis March Hatch and <a href="/wiki/William_Ansel_Kinney" title="William Ansel Kinney">William Ansel Kinney</a>. After negotiations in June 1897, Secretary of State <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_Sherman_(politician)" title="John Sherman (politician)">John Sherman</a> agreed to a treaty of annexation with these representatives of the Republic of Hawaii.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[80]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Senate" title="U.S. Senate">U.S. Senate</a> never ratified the treaty. Despite the opposition of most native Hawaiians,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[81]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Newlands_Resolution" title="Newlands Resolution">Newlands Resolution</a> was used to annex the Republic to the U.S.; it became the <a href="/wiki/Territory_of_Hawaii" title="Territory of Hawaii">Territory of Hawaii</a>. The Newlands Resolution was passed by the House on June 15, 1898, by 209 votes in favor to 91 against, and by the Senate on July 6, 1898, by a vote of 42 to 21.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[82]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[83]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[84]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1900, Hawaii was granted self-governance and retained <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iolani_Palace" title="Iolani Palace"><span class="unicode">ʻ</span>Iolani Palace</a> as the territorial capitol building. Despite several attempts to become a state, Hawaii remained a territory for sixty years. Plantation owners and capitalists, who maintained control through financial institutions such as the <a href="/wiki/Big_Five_(Hawaii)" title="Big Five (Hawaii)">Big Five</a>, found territorial status convenient because they remained able to import cheap, foreign labor. Such immigration and labor practices were prohibited in many states.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[85]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[86]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:USS_SHAW_exploding_Pearl_Harbor_Nara_80-G-16871_2.jpg"><img alt="The USS Shaw explodes during the Japanese attack on Pearl Harbor." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1500" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/USS_SHAW_exploding_Pearl_Harbor_Nara_80-G-16871_2.jpg/220px-USS_SHAW_exploding_Pearl_Harbor_Nara_80-G-16871_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/USS_SHAW_exploding_Pearl_Harbor_Nara_80-G-16871_2.jpg/330px-USS_SHAW_exploding_Pearl_Harbor_Nara_80-G-16871_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/USS_SHAW_exploding_Pearl_Harbor_Nara_80-G-16871_2.jpg/440px-USS_SHAW_exploding_Pearl_Harbor_Nara_80-G-16871_2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:USS_SHAW_exploding_Pearl_Harbor_Nara_80-G-16871_2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Japanese <a href="/wiki/Attack_on_Pearl_Harbor" title="Attack on Pearl Harbor">attack on Pearl Harbor</a> in 1941 was the primary event that galvanized the United States into entering <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_immigration_to_Hawaii" title="Puerto Rican immigration to Hawaii">Puerto Rican immigration to Hawaii</a> began in 1899 when Puerto Rico's sugar industry was devastated by two hurricanes, causing a worldwide shortage of sugar and a huge demand for sugar from Hawaii. Hawaiian <a href="/wiki/Sugarcane" title="Sugarcane">sugarcane</a> <a href="/wiki/Sugar_plantations_in_Hawaii" title="Sugar plantations in Hawaii">plantation</a> owners began to recruit experienced, unemployed laborers in Puerto Rico. Two waves of <a href="/wiki/Korean_immigration_to_Hawaii" title="Korean immigration to Hawaii">Korean immigration to Hawaii</a> occurred in the 20th century. The first wave arrived between 1903 and 1924; the second wave began in 1965 after President <a href="/wiki/Lyndon_B._Johnson" title="Lyndon B. Johnson">Lyndon B. Johnson</a> signed the <a href="/wiki/Immigration_and_Nationality_Act_of_1965" title="Immigration and Nationality Act of 1965">Immigration and Nationality Act of 1965</a> which removed racial and national barriers and resulted in significantly altering the demographic mix in the U.S.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[87]</a></sup></p>
<p>O<span class="unicode">ʻ</span>ahu was the target of a surprise <a href="/wiki/Attack_on_Pearl_Harbor" title="Attack on Pearl Harbor">attack on Pearl Harbor</a> by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Imperial_Japan" title="Imperial Japan">Imperial Japan</a> on December 7, 1941. The attack on Pearl Harbor and other military and naval installations, carried out by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Warplane" title="Warplane">aircraft</a> and by <a href="/wiki/Midget_submarine" title="Midget submarine">midget submarines</a>, brought the United States into <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>.</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span id="Political_changes_of_1954_–_the_State_of_Hawaii_(1959–present)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_changes_of_1954_.E2.80.93_the_State_of_Hawaii_.281959.E2.80.93present.29">Political changes of 1954 – the State of Hawaii (1959–present)</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Democratic_Revolution_of_1954_(Hawaii)" title="Democratic Revolution of 1954 (Hawaii)">Democratic Revolution of 1954 (Hawaii)</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Hawaiian_sovereignty_movement_groups#Modern_.E2.80.93_Sovereignty_Organizations_.281960s.E2.80.93present.29" title="List of Hawaiian sovereignty movement groups">List of Hawaiian sovereignty movement groups § Modern – Sovereignty Organizations (1960s–present)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Food-Hawaii-Canning._Native_girls_packing_pineapple_into_cans._-_NARA_-_522863.tif"><img alt="Three young women pack pineapples into cans in 1928." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2418" data-file-width="3000" height="177" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Food-Hawaii-Canning._Native_girls_packing_pineapple_into_cans._-_NARA_-_522863.tif/lossy-page1-220px-Food-Hawaii-Canning._Native_girls_packing_pineapple_into_cans._-_NARA_-_522863.tif.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Food-Hawaii-Canning._Native_girls_packing_pineapple_into_cans._-_NARA_-_522863.tif/lossy-page1-330px-Food-Hawaii-Canning._Native_girls_packing_pineapple_into_cans._-_NARA_-_522863.tif.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Food-Hawaii-Canning._Native_girls_packing_pineapple_into_cans._-_NARA_-_522863.tif/lossy-page1-440px-Food-Hawaii-Canning._Native_girls_packing_pineapple_into_cans._-_NARA_-_522863.tif.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Food-Hawaii-Canning._Native_girls_packing_pineapple_into_cans._-_NARA_-_522863.tif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Prior to the postwar labor movement, Hawaii was governed by plantation owners. Here, three young women pack pineapples into cans in 1928.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the 1950s, the power of the plantation owners was broken by the descendants of immigrant laborers, who were born in Hawaii and were U.S. citizens. They voted against the <a href="/wiki/Hawaii_Republican_Party" title="Hawaii Republican Party">Hawaii Republican Party</a>, strongly supported by plantation owners. The new majority voted for the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_of_Hawaii" title="Democratic Party of Hawaii">Democratic Party of Hawaii</a>, which dominated territorial and state politics for more than 40 years. Eager to gain full representation in Congress and the Electoral College, residents actively campaigned for statehood. In Washington there was talk that Hawaii would be a Republican Party stronghold so it was matched with the admission of Alaska, seen as a Democratic Party stronghold. These predictions turned out to be inaccurate; today, Hawaii votes Democratic predominately, and Alaska votes Republican.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[90]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[91]</a></sup></p>
<p>In March 1959, Congress passed the <a href="/wiki/Hawaii_Admission_Act" title="Hawaii Admission Act">Hawaii Admission Act</a>, which U.S. President <a href="/wiki/Dwight_D._Eisenhower" title="Dwight D. Eisenhower">Dwight D. Eisenhower</a> signed into law.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[92]</a></sup> The act excluded <a href="/wiki/Palmyra_Atoll" title="Palmyra Atoll">Palmyra Atoll</a> from statehood; it had been part of the Kingdom and Territory of Hawaii. On June 27, 1959, a referendum asked residents of Hawaii to vote on the statehood bill; 94.3% voted in favor of statehood and 5.7% opposed it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-celebrating-50-years-of-statehood_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-celebrating-50-years-of-statehood-95">[93]</a></sup> The referendum asked voters to choose between accepting the Act and remaining a U.S. territory. The United Nations' <a href="/wiki/Special_Committee_on_Decolonization" title="Special Committee on Decolonization">Special Committee on Decolonization</a> later removed Hawaii from <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_list_of_Non-Self-Governing_Territories" title="United Nations list of Non-Self-Governing Territories">its list of non-self-governing territories</a>.</p>
<p>After attaining statehood, Hawaii quickly modernized through construction and a rapidly growing tourism economy. Later, state programs promoted Hawaiian culture.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Avoid_weasel_words" title="Wikipedia:Avoid weasel words"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too vague attribution or weasel words. (March 2015)">which?</span></a></i>]</sup> The <a href="/wiki/1978_Hawaii_State_Constitutional_Convention" title="1978 Hawaii State Constitutional Convention">Hawaii State Constitutional Convention of 1978</a> created institutions such as the <a href="/wiki/Office_of_Hawaiian_Affairs" title="Office of Hawaiian Affairs">Office of Hawaiian Affairs</a> to promote indigenous language and culture.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Population">Population</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hawaii_population_map.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="600" height="250" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Hawaii_population_map.png/250px-Hawaii_population_map.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Hawaii_population_map.png/375px-Hawaii_population_map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Hawaii_population_map.png/500px-Hawaii_population_map.png 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hawaii_population_map.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Population density map of the Hawaiian islands.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Hawaii_statistical_areas" title="Hawaii statistical areas">Hawaii statistical areas</a></div>
<p>After Europeans and mainland Americans first arrived during the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hawaii" title="Kingdom of Hawaii">Kingdom of Hawaii</a> period, the overall population of Hawaii, until that time composed solely of indigenous Hawaiians, fell dramatically. The indigenous Hawaiian population succumbed to foreign diseases, declining from 300,000 in the 1770s, to 60,000 in the 1850s, to 24,000 in 1920. The population of Hawaii began to finally increase after an influx of primarily Asian settlers that arrived as migrant laborers at the end of the 19th<span class="nowrap"> </span>century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[94]</a></sup></p>
<p>The unmixed indigenous Hawaiian population has still not restored itself to its 300,000 pre-contact level. As of 2010, only 156,000 persons declared themselves to be of Native Hawaiian only ancestry, just over half of the pre-contact level Native Hawaiian population, although an additional 371,000 persons declared themselves to possess Native Hawaiian ancestry in combination with one or more other races (including other Polynesian groups, but mostly Asian and/or Caucasian).</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">United States Census Bureau</a> estimates the population of Hawaii was 1,431,603 on July 1, 2015; an increase of 5.2% since the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">2010 United States Census</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PopEstUS_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-PopEstUS-97">[95]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hawaii&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Hawaii had an estimated population of 1,431,603; an increase of 12,042 from the previous year and an increase of 71,302 (5.2%) since 2010. This includes a natural increase of 48,111 (96,028 births minus 47,917 deaths) and an increase due to net migration of 16,956 people into the state. Immigration from outside the United States resulted in a net increase of 30,068; migration within the country produced a net loss of 13,112 people.</p>
<p>The center of population of Hawaii is located between the two islands of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/O%27ahu" title="O'ahu">O'ahu</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moloka%27i" title="Moloka'i">Moloka'i</a>. Large numbers of Native Hawaiians have moved to <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas" title="Las Vegas">Las Vegas</a>, which has been called the "ninth island" of Hawaii.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[97]</a></sup></p>
<p>Hawaii has a <i>de facto</i> population of over 1.4<span class="nowrap"> </span>million, due in part to a large number of military personnel and tourist residents. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/O%27ahu" title="O'ahu">O'ahu</a> is the most populous island; it has the highest population density with a resident population of just under one million in 597 square miles (1,546 km<sup>2</sup>), approximately 1,650 people per square mile.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[c]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Hawaii's 1.4<span class="nowrap"> </span>million residents, spread across 6,000 square miles (15,500 km<sup>2</sup>) of land, result in an average population density of 188.6 persons per square mile.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[98]</a></sup> The state has a lower population density than <a href="/wiki/Ohio" title="Ohio">Ohio</a> and <a href="/wiki/Illinois" title="Illinois">Illinois</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USCB_density_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-USCB_density-102">[99]</a></sup></p>
<p>The average projected lifespan of people born in Hawaii in 2000 is 79.8 years; 77.1 years if male, 82.5 if female—longer than the average lifespan of any other <a href="/wiki/U.S._state" title="U.S. state">U.S. state</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[100]</a></sup> As of 2011<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hawaii&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> the U.S. military reported it had 42,371 personnel on the islands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hawaii_mil_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hawaii_mil-104">[101]</a></sup></p>

<p>According to the 2010 United States Census, Hawaii had a population of 1,360,301. The state's population identified as 38.6% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian_American" title="Asian American">Asian</a>; 24.7% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_American" title="White American">White</a> (22.7% Non-Hispanic White Alone); 23.6% from two or more races; 10.0% Native Hawaiians and other Pacific Islanders; 8.9% <a href="/wiki/Hispanic_and_Latino_Americans" title="Hispanic and Latino Americans">Hispanics</a> and Latinos of any race; 1.6% Black or African American; 1.2% from some other race; and 0.3% Native American and Alaska Native.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hawaii_QuickFacts_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hawaii_QuickFacts-107">[104]</a></sup></p>
